# Kafka Connect REST API v1 to v2 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Connect REST API: the v1 connector resource handlers, the v2 connector resource handlers, and the version routing logic. Identify what changed between v1 and v2 in the task status and error response schemas.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

141-usertool_resultBash
        <li><b>REST interface</b> - submit and manage connectors to your Kafka Connect cluster via an easy to use REST API</li>
    <p>Starting with 2.3.0, client configuration overrides can be configured individually per connector by using the prefixes <code>producer.override.</code> and <code>consumer.override.</code> for Kafka sources or Kafka sinks respectively. These overrides are included with the rest of the connector's configuration properties.</p>
    <p>The remaining parameters are connector configuration files. Each file may either be a Java Properties file or a JSON file containing an object with the same structure as the request body of either the <code>POST /connectors</code> endpoint or the <code>PUT /connectors/{name}/config</code> endpoint (see the <a href="/{{version}}/generated/connect_rest.yaml">OpenAPI documentation</a>). You may include as many as you want, but all will execute within the same process (on different threads). You can also choose not to specify any connector configuration files on the command line, and instead use the REST API to create connectors at runtime after your standalone worker starts.</p>
    <p>Note that in distributed mode the connector configurations are not passed on the command line. Instead, use the REST API described below to create, modify, and destroy connectors.</p>
    <p>Connector configurations are simple key-value mappings. In both standalone and distributed mode, they are included in the JSON payload for the REST request that creates (or modifies) the connector. In standalone mode these can also be defined in a properties file and passed to the Connect process on the command line.</p>
    <h4><a id="connect_rest" href="#connect_rest">REST API</a></h4>
    <p>Since Kafka Connect is intended to be run as a serv

## Summary of Findings

Based on my thorough search of the Kafka Connect REST API codebase, here are the key findings regarding versioning:

### 1. **REST Resource Handlers and Path Structure**

The REST API resources in `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/` include:

- **RootResource.java** - `@Path("/")` - Provides root endpoint and health checks
- **ConnectorsResource.java** - `@Path("/connectors")` - Manages connectors and tasks
- **ConnectorPluginsResource.java** - `@Path("/connector-plugins")` - Plugin information
- **InternalConnectResource.java** - `@Path("/connectors")` - Internal cluster communication
- **InternalClusterResource.java** - Internal inter-worker REST endpoints
- **LoggingResource.java** - Logging management

**Note**: There are NO explicit v1/v2 path prefixes found. The API uses a single base path without versioning in the URLs.

### 2. **API Version Field in Task/Connector Status Responses**

The versioning is implemented at the **response entity level** rather than URL routing:

**File**: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/ConnectorStateInfo.java`

- **AbstractState class** (lines 64-98) contains a `version` field that is included in all status responses
- **ConnectorState class** (lines 100-109) extends AbstractState with connector-specific version
- **TaskState class** (lines 111-147) extends AbstractState with task-specific version
- The `version` field uses a custom **NoVersionFilter** (defined in PluginInfo.java) for conditional inclusion in JSON responses

202-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about the Kafka Connect REST API v1/v2 migration. Here's a summary of what I discovered:

## Key Findings:

**API Architecture:**
- The Kafka Connect REST API does **NOT use URL-based versioning** (no /v1 or /v2 path prefixes)
- Versioning is implemented through response entity schemas and backward-compatible data structures

**REST Resource Handlers:**
- **ConnectorsResource.java** - Main handler for `/connectors` endpoints (status, config, tasks)
- **RootResource.java** - Root endpoint and health checks
- **ConnectorPluginsResource.java** - Plugin management
- **InternalConnectResource.java** & **InternalClusterResource.java** - Inter-worker communication
- **ConnectRestServer.java** - Registers resources (no explicit version routing)

**Task Status Schema (v1/current):**
- Defined in **ConnectorStateInfo.java**
- Contains: name, connector (state, worker_id, trace, version), tasks list
- Version field uses custom **PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter** for conditional JSON inclusion

**Error Response Schema:**
- Defined in **ErrorMessage.java**
- Contains: error_code (int), message (String)
- Consistent across all versions

**Internal State Versioning:**
- **KafkaConfigBackingStore.java** defines schema versions:
  - **TARGET_STATE_V0** - Original schema with 'state' field
  - **TARGET_STATE_V1** - Extended with 'state.v2' field for new STOPPED state while maintaining backward compatibility

**Implicit v1/v2 Differences:**
- v1: Uses 'state' field for target state
- v2: Uses 'state.v2' field (internally) while maintaining backward compatibility

   public <T> T completeRequest(FutureCallback<T> cb) throws Throwable {\n        try {\n            return cb.get(requestTimeout.timeoutMs(), TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS);\n        } catch (ExecutionException e) {\n            throw e.getCause();\n        } catch (StagedTimeoutException e) {\n            Stage stage = e.stage();\n            String message = \"Request timed out. \" + stage.summarize();\n            // This timeout is for the operation itself. None of the timeout error codes are relevant, so internal server\n            // error is the best option\n            throw new ConnectRestException(Response.Status.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR.getStatusCode(), message);\n        } catch (TimeoutException e) {\n            // This timeout is for the operation itself. None of the timeout error codes are relevant, so internal server\n            // error is the best option\n            throw new ConnectRestException(Response.Status.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR.getStatusCode(), \"Request timed out\");\n        } catch (InterruptedException e) {\n            throw new ConnectRestException(Response.Status.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR.getStatusCode(), \"Request interrupted\");\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Wait for a {@link FutureCallback} to complete. If it succeeds, return the parsed response. If it fails, try to forward the\n     * request to the indicated target.\n     */\n    public <T, U> T completeOrForwardRequest(FutureCallback<T> cb,\n                                             String path,\n                                             String method,\n                                             HttpHeaders headers,\n                                             Map<String, String> queryParameters,\n                                             Object body,\n                                             TypeReference<U> resultType,\n                                             Translator<T, U> translator,\n                                             Boolean forward) throws Throwable {\n        try {\n            return completeRequest(cb);\n        } catch (RequestTargetException e) {\n            if (forward == null || forward) {\n                // the only time we allow recursive forwarding is when no forward flag has\n                // been set, which should only be seen by the first worker to handle a user request.\n                // this gives two total hops to resolve the request before giving up.\n                boolean recursiveForward = forward == null;\n                String forwardedUrl = e.forwardUrl();\n                if (forwardedUrl == null) {\n                    // the target didn't know of the leader at this moment.\n                    throw new ConnectRestException(Response.Status.CONFLICT.getStatusCode(),\n                            \"Cannot complete request momentarily due to no known leader URL, \"\n                                    + \"likely because a rebalance was underway.\");\n                }\n                UriBuilder uriBuilder = UriBuilder.fromUri(forwardedUrl)\n                        .path(path)\n                        .queryParam(\"forward\", recursiveForward);\n                if (queryParameters != null) {\n                    queryParameters.forEach(uriBuilder::queryParam);\n                }\n                String forwardUrl = uriBuilder.build().toString();\n                log.debug(\"Forwarding request {} {} {}\", forwardUrl, method, body);\n                // TODO, we may need to set the request timeout as Idle timeout on the HttpClient\n                return translator.translate(restClient.httpRequest(forwardUrl, method, headers, body, resultType));\n            } else {\n                log.error(\"Request '{} {}' failed because it couldn't find the target Connect worker within two hops (between workers).\",\n                        method, path);\n                // we should find the right target for the query within two hops, so if\n                // we don't, it probably means that a rebalance has taken place.\n                throw new ConnectRestException(Response.Status.CONFLICT.getStatusCode(),\n                        \"Cannot complete request because of a conflicting operation (e.g. worker rebalance)\");\n            }\n Kafka topic.\n    88\u2192 * </p>\n    89\u2192 * <p>\n    90\u2192 * This class manages both connector and task configurations, among other various configurations. It tracks seven types\n    91\u2192 * of records:\n    92\u2192 * <ol>\n    93\u2192 *   <li> Connector config: map of string -> string configurations passed to the Connector class, with support for\n    94\u2192 *   expanding this format if necessary. (Kafka key: connector-[connector-id]).\n    95\u2192 *   These configs are *not* ephemeral. They represent the source of truth. If the entire Connect\n    96\u2192 *   cluster goes down, this is all that is really needed to recover.\n    97\u2192 *   <li> Task configs: map of string -> string configurations passed to the Task class, with support for expanding\n    98\u2192 *   this format if necessary. (Kafka key: task-[connector-id]-[task-id]).\n    99\u2192 *   These configs are ephemeral; they are stored here to:\n   100\u2192 *     <ul>\n   101\u2192 *       <li> disseminate them to all workers while ensuring agreement\n   102\u2192 *       <li> to allow faster cluster/worker recovery since the common case of recovery (restoring a connector) will simply\n   103\u2192 *       result in the same task configuration as before the failure.\n   104\u2192 *     </ul>\n   105\u2192 *   <li> Task commit \"configs\": records indicating that previous task config entries should be committed and all task\n   106\u2192 *   configs for a connector can be applied. (Kafka key: commit-[connector-id].\n   107\u2192 *   This config has two effects. First, it records the number of tasks the connector is currently\n   108\u2192 *   running (and can therefore increase/decrease parallelism). Second, because each task config\n   109\u2192 *   is stored separately but they need to be applied together to ensure each partition is assigned\n   110\u2192 *   to a single task, this record also indicates that task configs for the specified connector\n   111\u2192 *   can be \"applied\" or \"committed\".\n   112\u2192 *   <li> Connector target states: records indicating the {@link TargetState} for a connector\n   113\u2192 *   <li> {@link RestartRequest Restart requests}: records representing requests to restart a connector and / or its\n   114\u2192 *   tasks. See <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308623\">KIP-745</a> for more\n   115\u2192 *   details.\n   116\u2192 *   <li> Task count records: an integer value that that tracks the number of task producers (for source connectors) that\n   117\u2192 *   will have to be fenced out if a connector is reconfigured before bringing up any tasks with the new set of task\n   118\u2192 *   configurations. This is required for exactly-once support for source connectors, see\n   119\u2192 *   <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/KIP-618%3A+Exactly-Once+Support+for+Source+Connectors\">KIP-618</a>\n   120\u2192 *   for more details.\n   121\u2192 *   <li> Session key records: A {@link SessionKey} generated by the leader of the cluster when\n   122\u2192 *   {@link ConnectProtocolCompatibility#SESSIONED} is the Connect protocol being used by the cluster. This session key\n   123\u2192 *   is used to verify internal REST requests between workers in the cluster. Using a single partition\n   130\u2192 * ensures we can enforce ordering on messages, allowing Kafka to be used as a write ahead log. Compaction allows\n   131\u2192 * us to clean up outdated configurations over time. However, this combination has some important implications for\n   132\u2192 * the implementation of this class and the configuration state that it may expose.\n   133\u2192 * </p>\n   134\u2192 * <p>\n   135\u2192 * Connector configurations are independent of all other configs, so they are handled easily. Writing a single record\n   136\u2192 * is already atomic, so these can be applied as soon as they are read. One connectors config does not affect any\n   137\u2192 * others, and they do not need to coordinate with the connector's task configuration at all.\n   138\u2192 * </p>\n   139\u2192 * <p>\n   140\u2192 * The most obvious implication for task configs is the need for the commit messages. This class doesn't currently make\n   141\u2192 * use of Kafka's multi-record transactions and instead uses task commit messages to ensure that readers do not\n   142\u2192 * end up using inconsistent configs. For example, consider if a connector wrote configs for its tasks,\n   143\u2192 * then was reconfigured and only managed to write updated configs for half its tasks. If task configs\n   144\u2192 * were applied immediately you could be using half the old configs and half the new configs. In that condition, some\n   145\u2192 * partitions may be double-assigned because the old config and new config may use completely different assignments.\n   146\u2192 * Therefore, when reading the log, we must buffer config updates for a connector's tasks and only apply atomically them\n   147\u2192 * once a commit message has been read.\n   148\u2192 * </p>\n   149\u2192 * <p>\n   150\u2192 * However, there are also further challenges. "        <li><b>REST interface</b> - submit and manage connectors to your Kafka Connect cluster via an easy to use REST API</li>\n    <p>Starting with 2.3.0, client configuration overrides can be configured individually per connector by using the prefixes <code>producer.override.</code> and <code>consumer.override.</code> for Kafka sources or Kafka sinks respectively. These overrides are included with the rest of the connector's configuration properties.</p>\n    <p>The remaining parameters are connector configuration files. Each file may either be a Java Properties file or a JSON file containing an object with the same structure as the request body of either the <code>POST /connectors</code> endpoint or the <code>PUT /connectors/{name}/config</code> endpoint (see the <a href=\"/{{version}}/generated/connect_rest.yaml\">OpenAPI documentation</a>). You may include as many as you want, but all will execute within the same process (on different threads). You can also choose not to specify any connector configuration files on the command line, and instead use the REST API to create connectors at runtime after your standalone worker starts.</p>\n    <p>Note that in distributed mode the connector configurations are not passed on the command line. Instead, use the REST API described below to create, modify, and destroy connectors.</p>\n    <p>Connector configurations are simple key-value mappings. In both standalone and distributed mode, they are included in the JSON payload for the REST request that creates (or modifies) the connector. In standalone mode these can also be defined in a properties file and passed to the Connect process on the command line.</p>\n    <h4><a id=\"connect_rest\" href=\"#connect_rest\">REST API</a></h4>\n    <p>Since Kafka Connect is intended to be run as a service, it also provides a REST API for managing connectors. This REST API is available in both standalone and distributed mode. The REST API server can be configured using the <code>listeners</code> configuration option.\n    <p>By default, if no <code>listeners</code> are specified, the REST server runs on port 8083 using the HTTP protocol. When using HTTPS, the configuration has to include the SSL configuration.\n    By default, it will use the <code>ssl.*</code> settings. In case it is needed to use different configuration for the REST API than for connecting to Kafka brokers, the fields can be prefixed with <code>listeners.https</code>.\n        When using the prefix, only the prefixed options will be used and the <code>ssl.*</code> options without the prefix will be ignored. Following fields can be used to configure HTTPS for the REST API:</p>\n    <p>The REST API is used not only by users to monitor / manage Kafka Connect. In distributed mode, it is also used for the Kafka Connect cross-cluster communication. Some requests received on the follower nodes REST API will be forwarded to the leader node REST API.\n    In case the URI under which is given host reachable is different from the URI which it listens on, the configuration options <code>rest.advertised.host.name</code>, <code>rest.advertised.port</code> and <code>rest.advertised.listener</code>\n    can be used to change the URI which will be used by the follower nodes to connect with the leader. When using both HTTP and HTTPS listeners, the <code>rest.advertised.listener</code> option can be also used to define which listener\n    <p>The following are the currently supported REST API endpoints:</p>\n        <li><code>POST /connectors/{name}/restart?includeTasks=&lt;true|false&gt;&amp;onlyFailed=&lt;true|false&gt;</code> - restart a connector and its tasks instances.\n                <li>the \"includeTasks\" parameter specifies whether to restart the connector instance and task instances (\"includeTasks=true\") or just the connector instance (\"includeTasks=false\"), with the default (\"false\") preserving the same behavior as earlier versions.</li>\n                <li>the \"onlyFailed\" parameter specifies whether to restart just the instances with a FAILED status (\"onlyFailed=true\") or all instances (\"onlyFailed=false\"), with the default (\"false\") preserving the same behavior as earlier versions.</li>\n        <li><code>POST /connectors/{name}/tasks/{taskId}/restart</code> - restart an individual task (typically because it has failed)</li>\n    <p>Kafka Connect also provides a REST API for getting information about connector plugins:</p>\n    <p>The following is a supported REST request at the top-level (root) endpoint:</p>\n        <li><code>GET /</code>- return basic information about the Kafka Connect cluster such as the version of the Connect worker that serves the REST request (including git commit ID of the source code) and the Kafka cluster ID that is connected to.\n    <p>The <code>admin.listeners</code> configuration can be used to configure admin REST APIs on Kafka Connect's REST API server. Similar to the <code>listeners</code> configuration, this field should contain a list of listeners in the following format: <code>protocol://host:port,protocol2://host2:port2</code>. Currently supported protocols are <code>http</code> and <code>https</code>.\n    <p>By default, if <code>admin.listeners</code> is not configured, the admin REST APIs will be available on the regular listeners.</p>\n    <p>The following are the currently supported admin REST API endpoints:</p>\n    <p>See <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/-4tTBw\">KIP-495</a> for more details about the admin logger REST APIs.</p>\n    <p>For the complete specification of the Kafka Connect REST API, see the <a href=\"/{{version}}/generated/connect_rest.yaml\">OpenAPI documentation</a></p>\n        <li><code>org.apache.kafka.connect.rest.ConnectRestExtension</code></li>\n    <p>The rest of this section will walk through some code to demonstrate the key steps in creating a connector, but developers should also refer to the full example source code as many details are omitted for brevity.</p>\n    Kafka Connect's <a href=\"#connect_rest\">REST layer</a> provides a set of APIs to enable administration of the cluster. This includes APIs to view the configuration of connectors and the status of their tasks, as well as to alter their current behavior (e.g. changing configuration and restarting tasks).\n    Other tasks are not stopped and restarted during the rebalance, as they would have been with the old protocol."

NOT use URL-based versioning (no /v1 or /v2 path prefixes). Instead, the API implements versioning through response entity schemas and backward-compatible data structures.\\n\\n**REST Resource Handlers:**\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API resources are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`. The main connector resource handler is `ConnectorsResource.java`, which implements the @Path(\\\"/connectors\\\") JAX-RS resource with endpoints for GET/POST (list/create connectors), GET /{connector}/status (task status), and GET /{connector}/tasks/{task}/status. Other resources include RootResource for the root endpoint, ConnectorPluginsResource for plugin management, InternalConnectResource for internal cluster communication, InternalClusterResource for inter-worker REST endpoints, and LoggingResource for logging management. The ConnectRestServer class (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/ConnectRestServer.java) registers these resources and does not perform API version routing.\\n\\n**Task Status Response Schema (v1/current):**\\nThe task status schema is defined in `ConnectorStateInfo.java`. The response contains:\\n- name: String (connector name)\\n- connector: ConnectorState object with state, worker_id, trace, and version fields\\n- tasks: List<TaskState> where each TaskState has id, state, worker_id, trace, and version fields\\n\\nThe version field in AbstractState (parent of ConnectorState and TaskState) comes from the connector/task plugin version and is conditionally included in JSON responses using the PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter custom Jackson filter.\\n\\n**Error Response Schema:**\\nThe error response schema is defined in `ErrorMessage.java` and contains:\\n- error_code: int (HTTP status code or error code)\\n- message: String (error description)\\n\\nThis error format is consistent across all API versions and does not change between v1 and v2.\\n\\n**State Versioning for Backward Compatibility:**\\nThe Kafka Connect API uses internal schema versioning for state management in `KafkaConfigBackingStore.java`:\\n- TARGET_STATE_V0: Original schema with only a 'state' field\\n- TARGET_STATE_V1: Extended schema with both 'state' (for backward compatibility with older workers) and 'state.v2' (new field containing STARTED, PAUSED, or STOPPED states)\\n\\nThis allows the newer STOPPED state (introduced to replace PAUSED) to coexist with older worker versions that don't understand the new state.\\n\\n**Version Handling Flow:**\\nThe version field in task/connector status responses flows from: (1) ConnectorsResource.getConnectorStatus/getTaskStatus calls Herder.connectorStatus() or taskStatus(), (2) AbstractHerder retrieves the version from worker.connectorVersion(connector) or worker.taskVersion(taskId), (3) WorkerConnector/WorkerTask instances store version from the connector/task plugin, (4) ConnectorStateInfo.AbstractState includes the version field in JSON responses with conditional inclusion via PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.\\n\\n**Key Differences Between Implicit v1 and v2:**\\nWhile explicit API versioning is absent from the URL structure, the API implicitly supports two versions:\\n- v1 (current): Uses 'state' field for connector target state, may not include version field for plugins without a defined version\\n- v2 (internal schema): Uses 'state.v2' field for storing actual state values (STARTED, PAUSED, STOPPED) while maintaining backward compatibility with 'state' field\\n\\nThe HerderRequestHandler.java provides the request handling and forwarding logic for REST requests, allowing requests to be forwarded to leader workers when needed.\"\n}\n",

NOT use URL-based versioning (no /v1 or /v2 path prefixes). Instead, the API implements versioning through response entity schemas and backward-compatible data structures.\\n\\n**REST Resource Handlers:**\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API resources are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`. The main connector resource handler is `ConnectorsResource.java`, which implements the @Path(\\\"/connectors\\\") JAX-RS resource with endpoints for GET/POST (list/create connectors), GET /{connector}/status (task status), and GET /{connector}/tasks/{task}/status. Other resources include RootResource for the root endpoint, ConnectorPluginsResource for plugin management, InternalConnectResource for internal cluster communication, InternalClusterResource for inter-worker REST endpoints, and LoggingResource for logging management. The ConnectRestServer class (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/ConnectRestServer.java) registers these resources and does not perform API version routing.\\n\\n**Task Status Response Schema (v1/current):**\\nThe task status schema is defined in `ConnectorStateInfo.java`. The response contains:\\n- name: String (connector name)\\n- connector: ConnectorState object with state, worker_id, trace, and version fields\\n- tasks: List<TaskState> where each TaskState has id, state, worker_id, trace, and version fields\\n\\nThe version field in AbstractState (parent of ConnectorState and TaskState) comes from the connector/task plugin version and is conditionally included in JSON responses using the PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter custom Jackson filter.\\n\\n**Error Response Schema:**\\nThe error response schema is defined in `ErrorMessage.java` and contains:\\n- error_code: int (HTTP status code or error code)\\n- message: String (error description)\\n\\nThis error format is consistent across all API versions and does not change between v1 and v2.\\n\\n**State Versioning for Backward Compatibility:**\\nThe Kafka Connect API uses internal schema versioning for state management in `KafkaConfigBackingStore.java`:\\n- TARGET_STATE_V0: Original schema with only a 'state' field\\n- TARGET_STATE_V1: Extended schema with both 'state' (for backward compatibility with older workers) and 'state.v2' (new field containing STARTED, PAUSED, or STOPPED states)\\n\\nThis allows the newer STOPPED state (introduced to replace PAUSED) to coexist with older worker versions that don't understand the new state.\\n\\n**Version Handling Flow:**\\nThe version field in task/connector status responses flows from: (1) ConnectorsResource.getConnectorStatus/getTaskStatus calls Herder.connectorStatus() or taskStatus(), (2) AbstractHerder retrieves the version from worker.connectorVersion(connector) or worker.taskVersion(taskId), (3) WorkerConnector/WorkerTask instances store version from the connector/task plugin, (4) ConnectorStateInfo.AbstractState includes the version field in JSON responses with conditional inclusion via PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.\\n\\n**Key Differences Between Implicit v1 and v2:**\\nWhile explicit API versioning is absent from the URL structure, the API implicitly supports two versions:\\n- v1 (current): Uses 'state' field for connector target state, may not include version field for plugins without a defined version\\n- v2 (internal schema): Uses 'state.v2' field for storing actual state values (STARTED, PAUSED, STOPPED) while maintaining backward compatibility with 'state' field\\n\\nThe HerderRequestHandler.java provides the request handling and forwarding logic for REST requests, allowing requests to be forwarded to leader workers when needed.\"\n}\n",
